--- Commit Message ---
LU-10948 llite: Introduce inode open heat counter

Initial framework to support detection of naive apps that
assume open-closes are "free" and proceed to open/close
same files between minute operations.

We will track number of file opens per inode and last time inode
was closed.

Initially we'll expose these controls:
llite/opencache_threshold_count - enables functionality and controls after how
                                  many opens open lock is requested
llite/opencache_threshold_ms    - if any reopen happens within this time (in
                                  ms), the open would trigger open lock request
llite/opencache_max_ms          - If last close was longer than this many ms
                                  ago - start counting opens from zero again

Once enough useful data is collected we can look into adding a heatmap
or another similar mechanism to better manage it and enable it
by default with sensible settings.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-06-03 20:54:45.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

(4 comments)

Should probably get a test case where the same file is opened 1000x and check the ldlm_enqueue RPC count to verify it didn't do 1000x enqueues?

--- Message (Oleg Drokin, 2019-06-03 23:13:34.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

(3 comments)

> (4 comments)
 > 
 > Should probably get a test case where the same file is opened 1000x
 > and check the ldlm_enqueue RPC count to verify it didn't do 1000x
 > enqueues?

Yes.

The problem at hand is I discovered whole openlock functionality is currently crippled by the code outside of opens taking PR as the read lock everywhere.

That means all those CW locks to hold the write open handles are cancelled left an right. It turns out even cat does stat nowadays which fetches a PR lock.

We converted all PR locks to CR in 1.x releases, but somehow 2.x are all on PR so that seems to be the first thing to tackle.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-04-27 08:38:10.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

(7 comments)

What would be even more useful I think is tracking how often this client and/or thread is re-opening the same files (i.e. decaying "hit rate" for open-cached files), so that this can optimize the open lock request to be done on the first open rather than waiting for "lock_after_opens" requests on each file before requesting the open lock.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-04-27 08:39:39.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

It's not really clear why this is WIP?  It seems like a useful optimization, we just some workload measurements to see what kind of improvements it shows.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-04-29 00:12:18.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

Note that patch https://review.whamcloud.com/19664 "LU-7915 llite: add a tunable to enable opencache" overlaps with this code a fair amount (it just adds a single tunable to enable/disable openlock for the whole node), so I think it is a subset of the functionality in this patch (which is more of a per-inode tunable).

One thing worth pointing out is that it already has a sanity test case that might be useful to include here.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2020-07-08 15:14:42.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18:

Requesting open locks just breaks to much functionality for Lustre, changelogs, HSM, LSOM etc. We should have this feature disabled by default and let the user decide to enable this.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-07-09 11:11:05.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18:

(1 comment)

> Requesting open locks just breaks to much functionality for
> Lustre, changelogs, HSM, LSOM etc. We should have this feature
> disabled by default and let the user decide to enable this.

I'm not so worried about test breakage just because of different behavior than when the test was first written, if it means that we are getting improved functionality.  Being able to cache the open on a client reduces the RPC count to the MDS for workloads that need it.  It may (partly) be that tests are failing because of the strange exponential growth of the heat?  3 opens would result in a heat of (1+2+3=6).

For LSOM, open cache doesn't really "break" LSOM, just makes the size more lazy to be stored on the MDT.  That isn't really an "error" because the file is still being modified by the client during this time, and the LSOM should be updated eventually on the real close.  

Similarly, for Changelogs, there will be at least one open record written, and even without opencache there is not strict accounting of opens in the Changelog.

I'm not sure how opencache interferes with HSM?

I think the affected tests could be fixed by adjusting the heat threshold for the tests where it matters.

--- Message (Misc Code Checks Robot (Gatekeeper helper), 2020-07-10 00:50:05.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18:

Code-wise looks good to me.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2020-07-25 21:15:36.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18:

(1 comment)

>Being able to cache the open on a client reduces the RPC count to the >MDS for workloads that need it.
...
>For LSOM, open cache doesn't really "break" LSOM, just makes the size >more lazy to be stored on the MDT.  That isn't really an "error" >because the file is still being modified by the client during this >time, and the LSOM should be updated eventually on the real close.  
>
>Similarly, for Changelogs, there will be at least one open record >written, and even without opencache there is not strict accounting of >opens in the Changelog.
>
>I'm not sure how opencache interferes with HSM?

Sorry not HSM but MDT striping. This patch caused corrupt directory being created which I saw. It seems you want this behavior to be more the general rule than the exception, such as handling a bad application that does a burst of opens. I'm thinking have a open happen more than every second is okay to not to cache the open lock.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2020-12-26 18:22:42.000000000) ---
Patch Set 22:

So the patch does work locally for me. This shows the heat for opens can vary. The question is how to handle this. We have 3 options:

1) set lock_above_open_heat to a higher number for test 806?
2) bump SBI_DEFAULT_LOCK_ABOVE_OPEN_HEAT?
3) Maintain the current behavior of never taking the open_lock and let
   sites make the choice to set this feature.

The question is how dependent are site on lazy stats since this is what this impacts.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2020-12-26 20:12:40.000000000) ---
Patch Set 22:

(6 comments)

I think lazy stats will be increasingly important once distros have newer file utils that use statx() for ls, so I don't think that should be broken for opencache. 

That said, I would _hope_ that lazy stats continue to work even if opencache is enabled, just a bit more lazy, until the cached open is flushed to the MDS. The "lfs getsom" command (or direct read of the "som" xattr) is *not* how applications will interact with LSOM, but rather via statx() that should get attrs from client cache if they are available, so it is just this test that needs to be fixed.

I don't think skipping the test completely is good either, because we want to ensure LSOM continues to work. 

My thought is something like "cancel_lru_locks mdc" in check_lsom_size() if opencache is enabled, and clean up check_lsom_data() to call check_lsom_size() to avoid the duplication, should allow this test to pass.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2021-03-26 20:26:52.000000000) ---
Patch Set 28:

(3 comments)

Previously someone asked that heat be used. In fact your open count + time span is basically a reimplementation of using heat. I only implemented because someone asked for it. As I said having THREE tunables to do this is going to be hated by the user / admins.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-03-26 20:29:41.000000000) ---
Patch Set 28: Code-Review-1

(9 comments)

> I expect this is going to be rejected since the demand was that
 > it would be heat based. Way not many knobs to turn which is will
 > turn off users as well.
 >
 > Patch Set 28: Code-Review-1

I don't think it is fair to pre-emptively reject a patch just because someone _else_ might reject it.  :-)

I agree that the tunables are not well named (see comments), but if it works OK "out of the box" then the number of tunables is less of an issue, and Oleg wants them to understand the range of useful behaviors.

I'm still of the opinion that decaying average (i.e file heat) is an well understood and sensible behavior, but I don't think we ever got to a point where this was hooked into that quite right, so I'm willing to step back and go with a simpler approach if we can make forward progress on this patch.

This "bursty open detection plus hard cliff" is not totally unrelated to decaying average, and not quite as good IMHO (essentially a square wave instead of a curve), but I'm at the point were I'd prefer to see _something_ landed.

I'm less of a fan of landing this feature completely disabled at the start of the release cycle, when we could actually enable it by default, get some useful experience over the next few months, and then update the tunables or disable it by default for the next release if there are real issues.
